Tristan de Montebello, ek speech ke ant mein audience members dwara unki performance ke overall assessment ke alava, is baare mein pal-pal live informational feedback bhi haasil kar sakte hain ki yeh moment-to-moment kaise chal raha hai. Kya woh joke kaam kiya? Kya meri story unhein bore kar rahi hai? Yeh kuch aisi cheez hai jise aap apni poori speech ke dauran bhatki hui nazaron (distracted glances) ya background chatter (piche ki baatcheet) mein spot kar sakte hain. Rock ka stand-up experiment bhi informational feedback ka ek type hai. Woh audience ke reaction ke aadhar par bata sakte hain ki kab koi khhas joke land hua ya nahi. Halanki, woh unhein yeh nahi bata sakte ki ise mazeed funnier banane ke liye kya karna hai—woh comedian hain, woh nahi.

Is tarah ka feedback haasil karna aasan hota hai jab aap kisi feedback srot tak real-time access paa sakte hain. Ek computer programmer jise error messages milte hain jab uske programs properly compile nahi hote, uske paas shayad yeh samajhne ke liye kaafi knowledge na ho ki woh kya galat kar rahi hai. Lekin jaise hi errors badhte hain ya kam hote hain, is par depend karte hue ki woh kya karti hai, woh un signals ka use apni problems ko fix karne ke liye kar sakti hai. Self-provided feedback (khud se milne wala feedback) bhi har jagah majood (ubiquitous) hai, aur kuch prayason mein yeh doosron se milne wale feedback jitna hi achha ho sakta hai. Paint karte waqt, aap simply ise dekh sakte hain aur ek ehsaas haasil kar sakte hain ki kya aapke brushstrokes us image ko convey karne mein add kar rahe hain ya detract (asar kam) kar rahe hain jise aap prastut karna chahte hain. Kyunki is tarah ka feedback aksar environment ke sath direct interaction se aata hai, yeh aksar teesre niyan, directness ke sath achha pair (mel) khata hai.

### Corrective Feedback: How Can You Fix What You’re Doing Wrong?

_(Corrective Feedback: Aap Jo Galat Kar Rhe Hain Use Kaise Fix Kar Sakte Hain?)_
Haasil karne ke liye sabse behtar tarah ka feedback corrective feedback hai. Yeh woh feedback hai jo aapko na keval yeh dikhata hai ki aap kya galat kar rahe hain balki yeh bhi ki ise fix kaise karna hai. Is tarah ka feedback aksar kevel ek coach, mentor, ya teacher ke zariye hi available hota hai. Halanki, kabhi-kabhi yeh automatically provide kiya ja sakta hai agar aap sahi study materials ka use kar rahe hain.

MIT Challenge ke dauran, maine apni zyaada tar practice assignments aur unke solutions ke beech aage-peeche jaakar ki, taaki jab maine ek problem khatam ki, toh mujhe na keval yeh dikhaya gaya ki maine ise sahi kiya tha ya galat balki exactly yeh bhi ki mera answer sahi wale se kaise different tha. Similarly, flash cards aur active recall ke doosre forms aapke guess karne ke baad kisi sawaal ka answer dikhakar corrective feedback provide karte hain.

Educators Maria Araceli Ruiz-Primo aur Susan M. Brookhart tark dete hain, “Sabse behtar feedback informative aur use haasil karne wale student(s) dwara usable (upyog karne yogya) hota hai. Optimal feedback majooda state aur desired learning state ke beech ka farq indicate karta hai AND students ko apni learning ko behtar banane ke liye ek step uthane mein madad karta hai.”

Is tarah ke feedback ka mukhya challenge yeh hai ki isme aam taur par ek teacher, expert, ya mentor tak access ki zarurat hoti hai jo aapki galtiyon ko pinpoint kar sake aur unhein aapke liye correct kar sake. Halanki, kabhi-kabhi merely informational ke upar corrective feedback hone ka added edge un logon ko dhoondhne ke liye required mehnat ke layak ho sakta hai. Tristan de Montebello ne apni public speaking performance mein madad ke liye Michael Gendler ke sath kaam kiya, aur usne unhein presentations mein un baareek weaknesses ko spot karne mein madad ki jo unke dwara khud ya mazeed broad feedback dene wale ek kam experienced audience member dwara unnoticed chali jaatin.

Is type ka feedback outcome feedback (jo yeh indicate nahi kar sakta ki kya behtar banana hai) aur informational feedback (jo yeh indicate kar sakta hai ki kya behtar banana hai lekin yeh nahi ki kaise) dono ko hara (trump) deta hai. Halanki, yeh unreliable bhi ho sakta hai. Tristan de Montebello ko ek speech deliver karne ke baad aksar virodhabhaasi salah (conflicting advice) milti thi; kuch audience members unhein slow hone ke liye kehte, jabki doosre kehte ki speed badhao. Yeh ek aisi situation bhi ho sakti hai jahan ek tutor ke liye pay karna useful ho sakta hai, kyunki woh insaan aapki galti ke exact nature ko spot kar sakta hai aur aapke part par kam struggle ke sath ise correct kar sakta hai. Ultralearning ki self-directed nature aapko is baat par convince nahi karni chahiye ki learning poori tarah se ek tanhaa prayas (solitary pursuit) ke roop mein sabse behtar ki jaati hai.

### Further Notes on Types of Feedback

_(Feedback Ke Types Par Mazeed Notes)_
Yahan kuch cheezein dhyan dene layak hain.

- Pehle, aapko saavdhaan rehne ki zarurat hai jab feedback ko ek weaker form se ek stronger form mein “upgrade” karne ki koshish kar rahe hon agar yeh actually possible na ho. Outcome feedback se informational feedback par switch karne ke liye, aap jo kar rahe hain uske per element ke aadhar par feedback ugalwane (elicit) kabil hona chahiye. Agar iske bajaye feedback aap jo kuch bhi kar rahe hain uske ek holistic assessment ke roop mein pradan kiya ja raha hai, toh ise informational feedback mein badalne ki koshish backfire kar sakti hai. Game designers is baare mein watch out karna jaante hain, kyunki play testers se yeh poochne par ki unhein game ke baare mein kya pasand nahi hai, aksar spurious (galat/nakli) results mil sakte hain: for example, unhein character ka color pasand nahi hai ya background music. Truth yeh hai, players game ko holistically evaluate kar rahe hote hain, isliye woh aksar is tarah ka feedback offer nahi kar sakte. Agar unke responses ise ek poore ke roop mein use karne se aate hain, na ki har ek aspect se individually, toh greater specificity (mazeed baareekiyon) ke liye poochna feedback dene walon ki taraf se guesses (andaza lagane) ki taraf le ja sakta hai.
- Similarly, corrective feedback ke liye ek “correct” answer ya kisi recognized expert ke response ki zarurat hoti hai. Agar wahan koi expert ya koi single correct approach nahi hai, toh informational feedback ko corrective feedback mein badalne ki koshish aapke khilaf kaam kar sakti hai jab kisi galat badlav ko ek improvement ke roop mein suggest kiya jaye. De Montebello ne mujhse note kiya ki zyaada tar logon ne unhein jo salah di woh bahut zyaada useful nahi thi, lekin iski consistency (lagaatar bane rehna) thi. Agar unki speech ne har baar wildly different reactions ugalwaye (elicited), toh woh jaante the ki abhi bhi bahut saara kaam karna baki hai. Jab speech par kahin zyaada consistent comments milna shuru hue, toh woh jaante the ki woh kisi sahi raaste par hain. Yeh pradarshit karta hai ki ultralearning simply feedback ko maximize karne ke baare mein nahi hai balki useful jankari ko extract karne ke liye iske elements ko selectively ignore karna jaan'ne ke baare mein bhi hai. Feedback ke in different types ke niyamon (merits) ko samajhna, sath hi un preconditions ko bhi jo unhein possible banati hain, ek ultralearning project ke liye sahi strategy chun'ne ka ek bada hissa hai.

## How Quick Should Feedback Be?

_(Feedback Kitna Tez Hona Chahiye?)_

Feedback par research mein ek interesting question yeh hai ki yeh kitna tez (quick) hona chahiye. Kya aapko apni galtiyon ke baare mein immediate jankari milni chahiye ya kuch samay wait karna chahiye? In general, research ne laboratory se baahar ke settings mein immediate feedback ke superior hone ki taraf point kiya hai. James A. Kulik aur Chen-Lin C. Kulik feedback timing par sahitya (literature) ka moolyankan karte hain aur suggest karte hain ki “Actual classroom quizzes aur real learning materials ka upyog karne wale applied studies ne aam taur par immediate feedback ko delay ke mukable mazeed effective paaya hai.” Expertise researcher K. Anders Ericsson sahmat hain, immediate feedback ke paksh mein tark dete hue jab yeh galtiyon ko identify aur correct karne mein assist (madhad) karta hai aur jab yeh kisi ko feedback ke response mein revised apni performance ke ek corrected version ko execute karne kabil banata hai.

Interestingly, laboratory studies yeh dikhane ki taraf jhukte hain ki original task ke sath sahi response ki prastuti ko delay karna (delayed feedback) mazeed effective hota hai. Is result ka sabse simple explanation yeh hai ki sawaal aur answer ko phir se prastut karna jankari ke liye ek doosra, spaced exposure offer karta hai. Agar yeh explanation sahi tha, toh iska matlab sirf yeh hoga ki single exposure ke comparison mein aapki memory ko strengthen karne liye immediate feedback ko delayed review (ya mazeed testing) ke sath pair karna sabse behtar hai. Main spacing par aur yeh aapki memory par kaise impact daalata hai ispar agle chapter, retention mein mazeed cover karunga.

Scientific literature se feedback ki timing par superficially mixed results ke bavajood, main aam taur par faster feedback ka suggestion deta hoon. Yeh galtiyon ki ek tezi se recognition kabil banata hai. Halanki, is baat ka ek sambhavit risk (possible risk) hai ki yeh recommendation haath mein majood sawaal ka answer dene ya problem ko solve karne ki apni poori koshish karne se pehle hi feedback haasil karne mein badal (backslide) jaye. Feedback timing par shuruati studies learning par immediate feedback ka ek neutral ya negative impact dikhane ki taraf jhukti thin. Un studies mein, halanki, experimenters ne aksar subjects ko prompt ko poora bharne se pehle hi sahi answer dekhne ki ability de di thin. Uska matlab tha ki subjects ise retrieve karne ki koshish karne ke bajaye aksar sahi answer copy kar sakte the. Bahut jaldi feedback aapki retrieval practice ko effectively passive review mein badal sakta hai, jise hum pehle se jaante hain ki learning ke liye kam effective hai. Hard problems ke liye, main apne liye ek timer set karne ka suggestion deta hoon taaki aap sahi answer dekhne ke liye give up karne se pehle difficult problems par gehrai se sochne (think hard) ke liye encourage hon.

## How to Improve Your Feedback

_(Apne Feedback Ko Kaise Behtar Banayein)_

Abhi tak aap apni learning prayason ke liye feedback ka mahatva dekh chuke hain. Maine explain kiya hai ki kyun feedback, khhasakar jab doosron tak deliver kiya jata hai, kabhi-kabhi backfire kar sakta hai. Maine yeh bhi dikhaya hai ki kaise teen types—outcome, informational, aur corrective—ke paas different strengths hain aur un preconditions ko jo unhein effective banane liye jagah par hone ki zarurat hai. Ab main kuch concrete tactics par focus karna chahta hoon jinhein aap behtar feedback haasil karne liye apply kar sakte hain.

### Tactic 1: Noise Cancellation

_(Ranniti 1: Noise Cancellation [Shor Ko Hatana])_
Jab bhi aap feedback receive karte hain, toh wahan dono hone wale hain—ek **signal**—woh useful jankari jise aap process karna chahte hain—aur **noise (shor)**. Noise random factors ke kaaran hoti hai, jispar aapko behtar banane ki koshish karte waqt overreact nahi karna chahiye. Say aap articles likh rahe hain jinhein aap online post karte hain, apni writing ability ko behtar banane ki koshish karte hue. Unmein se zyaada tar bahut zyaada attention attract nahi karenge, aur jab woh karte hain, toh yeh aksar aapke control se baahar ke factors ke kaaran hota hai; for example, bas sahi insaan ise share kar deta hai, jisse yeh social networks par phhail (spill) jata hai. Aapki writing ki quality in factors ko chalati (drive) zaroor hai, lekin wahan kaafi randomness hoti hai ki aapko is baat ke liye saavdhaan rehna hoga ki ek single data point ke aadhar par apna poora approach na badlein.

Noise aapke craft ko behtar banane ki koshish karte waqt ek real problem hai kyunki aapko achhi tarah likhne ke baare mein same jankari haasil karne liye kahin zyaada kaam karne ki zarurat hoti hai. Feedback ke jin streams par aap dhayan dete hain unhein modify aur select karke, aap noise ko kam kar sakte hain aur mazeed signal paa sakte hain.

Audio processing mein use ki jaane wali ek noise-cancelling technique **filtering (chhan'na)** hai. Sound engineers jaante hain ki insani speech khhas frequencies ki range ke andar aane ki taraf jhukti hai, jabki white noise poore spectrum par hoti hai. Woh signal ko badha (boost) sakte hain, isliye, un frequencies ko amplify karke jo insani speech mein hoti hain aur baki sab ko shaant (quieting) karke. Aisa karne ka ek tarika **proxy signals** ko dekhna hai. Yeh exactly success ke barabar nahi hote, lekin yeh noisy data ke kuch hisse ko eliminate karne ki taraf jhukte hain. Blog writing ke liye, aisa karne ka ek tarika tracking code ka use karna hoga yeh figure out karne liye ki kitne percentage log aapke articles ko poora ant tak padhte hain. Yeh prove nahi karta ki aapki writing achhi hai, lekin yeh raw traffic data ke mukable kahin kam noisy hai.

### Tactic 2: Hitting the Difficulty Sweet Spot

_(Ranniti 2: Difficulty Ke Sweet Spot Ko Hit Karna)_
Feedback jankari (information) hai. Mazeed jankari barabar seekhne ke mazeed opportunities. Jankari ka ek scientific measure is baat par based hota hai ki aap kitni aasaani se predict kar sakte hain ki isme kaun sa message shamil hoga. Agar aap jaante hain ki success guaranteed hai, toh feedback khud koi jankari provide nahi karta; aap shuruat se hi jaante the ki yeh achha jayega. Achha feedback iska ulta karta hai. Ise predict karna bahut hard hota hai aur is tarah jab bhi aap ise receive karte hain yeh mazeed jankari deta hai.

Mukhya tarika jisse yeh aapki learning par impact daalata hai woh aapke samne majood difficulty ke zariye hai. Kai log sahaj roop se constant failure se bachte hain, kyunki isse milne wala feedback hamesha sahayak nahi hota. Halanki, iska ulta problem, bahut zyaada successful hona, mazeed vyapak (pervasive) hai. Ultralearners saavdhani se apne environment ko adjust karte hain taaki woh yeh predict karne kabil na hon ki woh succeed honge ya fail. Agar woh bahut zyaada baar fail hote hain, toh woh problem ko simplify kar dete hain taaki jab woh cheezon ko sahi kar rahe hon toh notice karna shuru kar sakein. Agar woh bahut kam fail hote hain, toh woh task ko harder ya apne standards ko mazeed strict bana denge taaki woh different approaches ke success mein bhed (distinguish) kar sakein. Basically, aapko aisi situations se bachne ki koshish karni chahiye jo aapko apni performance ke baare mein hamesha achha (ya bura) feel karwati hain.

### Tactic 3: Metafeedback

_(Ranniti 3: Metafeedback)_
Typical feedback performance assessment (moolyankan) hai: kisi quiz par aapka grade aapko is baare mein kuch batata hai ki aap material ko kitni achhi tarah jaante hain. Halanki, ek aur type ka feedback hai jo shayad isse bhi zyaada useful hai: **metafeedback**. Is tarah ka feedback aapki performance ke baare mein nahi hai balki aap seekhne ke liye jis strategy ka use kar rahe hain uski overall success ko evaluate karne ke baare mein hai.

Metafeedback ka ek important type aapki **learning rate (seekhne ki raftaar)** hai. Yeh aapko is baare mein jankari deta hai ki aap kitni tezi se seekh rahe hain, ya kam se kam aap apni skill ke ek aspect mein kitni tezi se behtar ho rahe hain. Chess players apne Elo ratings ki growth ko track kar sakte hain. LSAT studiers mock exams par apni improvements ko track can sakte hain. Language learners seekhi gayi vocabulary ya likhte ya bolte waqt ki gayi errors ko track kar sakte hain.

Aap is tool ka use do tareeqon se kar sakte hain.

- Ek yeh decide karne ke liye hai ki aapko kab us strategy par focus karna chahiye jise aap pehle se use kar rahe hain aur kab aapko doosre methods ke sath prayog (experiment) karna chahiye. Agar aapki learning rate ek boond (trickle) tak slow ho rahi hai, toh iska matlab ho sakta hai ki aap apne majooda approach ke sath ghatt-te pratiphal (diminishing returns) ko hit kar rahe hain aur different tarah ke drills, difficulties, ya environments se benefit paa sakte hain.
- Ek doosra tarika jisse aap metafeedback apply kar sakte hain woh do different study methods ko compare karke dekhna hai ki kaun sa behtar kaam karta hai. MIT Challenge ke dauran, main ek exam par khud par test lene se pehle different subtopics se questions ko split kar deta tha aur side by side different approaches try karta था. Kya sawaalon ke answers dene mein directly dive kar jana behtar kaam karta hai ya pehle mukhya concepts ko samajhne ki koshish mein thoda samay bitana? Akela tarika jisse aap jaan sakte hain woh apni khud ki learning rates ko test karna hai.

### Tactic 4: High-Intensity, Rapid Feedback

_(Ranniti 4: High-Intensity, Rapid Feedback)_
Kabhi-kabhi feedback ko behtar banane ka sabse aasan tarika simply iska bahut zyaada hissa kahin zyaada baar haasil karna hota hai. Yeh khhasakar tab sach hai jab learning ka default mode kam ya kam aane wale feedback (infrequent feedback) ko shamil karta hai. De Montebello ki public speaking ko behtar banane ki strategy mukhya roop se stage par zyaada tar speakers ke mukable kahin zyaada baar frequent exposure haasil karne par nirbhar thi. Lewis ka language immersion unhein unki pronunciation ke baare mein us point par jankari se expose karta hai jab zyaada tar students ne abhi tak ek word bhi nahi utthara hota. High-intensity, rapid feedback informational advantages offer karta hai, lekin zyaada tar advantage emotional bhi hota hai. Feedback receive karne ka darr aksar aapko kisi bhi cheez se zyaada peeche khinch sakta hai. Apne aap ko ek high-intensity, rapid feedback situation mein jhonk (throwing) kar, aap shuruat mein uncomfortable feel kar sakte hain, lekin aap us shuruati na-pasandi (initial aversion) ko usse kahin zyaada tezi se paar kar lenge jitna aap tab karte jab aap feedback haasil karne se pehle mahino ya saalon wait karte.

Aisi situation mein hona aapko mazeed aakramak roop se learning mein engage hone ke liye bhi uksata (provokes) hai jitna aap otherwise karte. Yeh jaan'na ki aapke kaam ko evaluate kiya jayega, apna best dene ke liye ek incredible motivator hai. High-intensity feedback ke liye commit karne ka yeh motivational angle aakhirkar isse pradan kiye jaane wale informational advantage se bada sabit ho sakta hai.

## Beyond Feedback

_(Feedback Se Pare)_

Feedback receive karna hamesha aasan nahi hota. Agar aap ise apne skills ke bajaye apne ego (aham) ke baare mein ek message ke roop mein process karte hain, toh ek mukke (punch) ko knockout banna aasan hai. Bhale hi feedback environment ko saavdhani se control karna taaki yeh maximally encouraging ho, ek aakarshak vikalp (tantalizing option) ho sakta hai, real life shayad hi kabhi aisa opportunity deti hai. Iske bajaye, behtar hai ki andar ghusein aur punches ko jaldi lein (take the punches early) taaki woh aapko count ke liye neeche na giraaein (don't put you down for the count). Bhale hi short-term feedback stressful ho sakta hai, ek baar jab aap ise receive karne ki habit mein aa jaate hain, toh bina bhavnatmak roop se overreact (overreacting emotionally) kiye ise process karna aasan ho jata hai. Ultralearners iska use apne advantage ke liye karte hain, apne aap ko massive amounts of feedback se expose karte hue taaki noise ko signal se strip away (hataya) ja sake.

Feedback aur isse pradan kiye jaane wali jankari, halanki, tabhi useful hai agar aap un lessons ko yaad rakhein jinhein yeh sikhati hai. Bhoolna insani fitrat (human nature) hai, isliye sirf seekhna hi kafi nahi hai; aapko jankari ko tikane (make the information stick) ki bhi zarurat hai. Yeh hamein ultralearning ke agle niyan tak le jata hai, **retention (barkarar rakhna/tikana)**, jisme hum un strategies par discuss karenge jo ensure karengi ki aapke dwara seekhe gaye lessons ko bhoola na jaye.

---

# Chapter 10 — Principle 7: Retention

### _(Niyam 7 — Retention: Ek Tooti Hui Balti Ko Mat Bharo)_

---

> _"Memory is the residue of thought."_
> _(Yaadashth [Memory] soch ka avashesh hai.)_
> — Daniel Willingham, cognitive psychologist

---

Belgium ke ek chote se city Louvain-la-Neuve mein, Nigel Richards ne abhi-abhi _World Scrabble Championships_ jeeti hai. Apne aap mein, yeh bahut zyaada hairan karne wala nahi hai. Richards ne pehle bhi teen baar yeh championship jeeti hai, aur game ke sath unka hunar aur unki ajeeb/rahasyamai personality (mysterious personality) dono ne unhein competitive Scrabble ke daires mein ek legend jaisa bana diya hai.

Is baar, halanki, badlav hai: is famous crossword game ke original English-language version ke bajaye, Richards ne _French World Championship_ jeeti hai. Yeh isse kahin zyaada harder carnama hai: zyaada tar English dictionary versions mein lagbhag 200,000 valid word entries hoti hain; French mein, ling-bhed wale nouns aur adjectives (gendered nouns and adjectives) aur vyapak kriya-roopon/rupakhhyan (copious conjugations) ke sath, lagbhag 386,000 valid word forms ke sath isse dugna hai. Aise carname ko anjam dena (pull off) kaafi remarkable hai, aur isse bhi zyaada ek simple fact ke kaaran: **Richards French nahi bolte.**

Richards, Christchurch, New Zealand mein paida hue aur pale-badhe ek engineer hain, jo ek unusual character hain. Apni lambi daadhi aur retro aviator sunglasses ke sath, woh Gandalf aur Napoleon Dynamite ke beech ke ek mix jaise dikhte hain. Scrabble mein unke skills, halanki, koi mazaak nahi hain. Game mein der se shuruat karne wale, unki mother ne unhein unki late twenties mein shuru karne ke liye prabandhit (encouraged) kiya tha, yeh kehte hue, “Nigel, chunki tum lafzon mein achhe nahi ho, toh tum is game mein behtar nahi hoge, lekin yeh tumhein busy (occupied) rakhega.” Un ashubh shuruaton (inauspicious beginnings) se Richards ne competitive Scrabble scene par dominate karna jaari rakkha hai. Kuch log toh yahan tak tark dete hain ki woh abhi tak ke sabse bade player ho sakte hain.

In case agar aap kisi gufa mein reh rahe hon (living under a rock), Scrabble crosswords banane par based hai. Har player ke paas ek bag se khinche gaye saat letter tiles hote hain, jinse words banane hote hain. Pech (catch) yeh hai ki words ko board par pehle se majood words ke sath link hona chahiye. Ek achha player banne ke liye ek vishal memory (voluminous memory) ki zarurat hoti hai, na keval un lafzon ki jinhein hum har din use karte hain balki un gudh lafzon (obscure words) ki bhi jo apni length ya unmein majood letters ke kaaran useful hote hain. Ek decent casual player jaldi se saare valid do-letter words seekh leta hai, jisme unusual words jaise “AA” (ek tarah ka lava) aur “OE” (Faroe Islands mein ek aandhi [windstorm]) shamil hain.

Tournament level par perform karne ke liye, halanki, lagbhag saare chhote words ko memorize karne ki zarurat hoti hai, sath hi lambe saat- aur aath-letter words ko bhi, kyunki agar ek player ek hi baari (turn) mein saare saat tiles use kar leta hai, toh ek extra fifty-point bonus milta hai (ya Scrabble jargon mein “bingo”). Memory, halanki, akeli required skill nahi hai. Doosre competitive games ki tarah, tournament Scrabble ek timing system ka use karta hai, isliye kushal players ko na keval letters ke ek jumbled set se valid words construct karne kabil hona chahiye balki jaldi se spaces dhoondhna aur calculate karna chahiye ki kaun se words sabse zyaada points score karenge. Is mamle mein, Richards ek master hain: tiles CDHLRN aur ek blank (jise kisi bhi letter ke liye use kiya ja sakta hai) diye jaane par, Richards ne obvious word _CHILDREN_ ko ignore kiya aur iske bajaye isse bhi zyaada scoring karne wala _CHLORODYNE_ banane ke liye multiple crosswords ko link kar diya.

Richards ki yeh vishishtata (virtuosity) sirf us mystery se mazeed badh (intensified) jaati hai jo iske chaaron taraf hai. Woh shaant hain aur zyaada tar apne aap mein rehte hain. Woh reporters ke sath saare interviews se mana kar dete hain aur shohrat (fame), kismat (fortune), ya yahan tak ki yeh explain karne mein poori tarah se uninterested lagte hain ki woh ise kaise karte hain. Unke ek saathi pratiyogi (fellow competitor), Bob Felt ne ek tournament mein Richards se takraate hue unki ek sanyasi jaisi shanti (monklike serenity) ko notice kiya, unhein kehte hue, “Jab main aapko dekhta hoon, main kabhi nahi bata sakta ki aap jeete hain ya haare hain.” “Aisa isliye hai kyunki mujhe parwah nahi hai” Richards ka ek-hi-sur (monotone) wala javab tha. Yahan tak ki Belgium mein unka compete karna, jisne unhein briefly international media ke spotlight mein khincha, Europe ke zariye ek cycling trip karne ke ek bahane ke roop mein kiya gaya tha. In fact, apni victory se pehle, unhone prepare karne mein sirf nau hafte bitaye the. Final match mein Gabon ke ek Francophone player, Schelick Ilagou Rekawe ko harane ke baad, unhein khade hokar badhai (standing ovation) di gayi lekin audience ko thank you kehne ke liye unhein ek translator ki zarurat padi.

## What Is Nigel Richards’s Secret?

_(Nigel Richards Ka Secret Kya Hai?)_

Main Nigel Richards ke baare mein jitna zyaada padhta gya, main utna hi mazeed utsuk (intrigued) hota gaya. Richards jitne mysterious the utne hi apni mnemonic (smaran-sahayak) kshamtayon mein incredible the. Woh dradhta se interviews ke opportunities ko ignore karte hain aur apne methods ke descriptions mein famously mukh-shakt/kam bolne wale (laconic) hain. Louvain-la-Neuve mein unki victory ke baad, ek reporter ne unse poocha ki kya unke paas un saare words ko memorize karne ke liye koi special methods hain. “Nahi” Richards ka ek-shabdiya (monosyllabic) javab tha. Phir bhi, bhale hi woh apni strategies ko publicly zahir (divulge) nahi karenge, shayad kuch dig (khoj) karne se clues mil sakein.

Pehli cheez jo maine discover ki woh yeh thi ki bhale hi Belgium mein Richards ki victory astounded (hairatangez) thi, yeh poori tarah se purv-nirdharit/nazeer ke bina (without precedent) nahi thi. Game ke doosre players ne competition ki bhasha mein fluent hue bina World Championships jeeti hain. Scrabble Thailand mein khhasakar popular hai, for instance, aur do purane world champions, Panupol Sujjayakorn aur Pakorn Nemitrmansuk, English mein fluent nahi hain. Kaaran simple hai: apni native tongue mein words yaad rakhna aur Scrabble mein words yaad rakhna different mnemonic carname hain. Spoken bhasha mein, ek word ka matlab, iska pronunciation, aur iska feel important hote hain. Scrabble mein, un cheezon se koi farq nahi padta; words bas letters ke combinations hain. Richards French Scrabble mein French bole bina jeet sakte the kyunki game English se bahut zyaada different nahi tha; unhein bas letters ke different patterns ko memorize karna tha. Ek native speaker ko ek advantage hota hai, beshak, kyunki kai spellings pehle se hi familiar hongi. Lekin memorize karne ke liye abhi bhi badi matra mein rahasyamai/gudh (arcane) aur anjaan words honge, aur letters ko valid board positions mein dobara arrange karne aur maximal points haasil karne ke liye calculate karne ki skill har us bhasha mein same rehti hai jisme Scrabble khela ja sakta hai.

Puzzle ka agla hissa jo maine discover kiya woh yeh tha ki Scrabble, it turns out, akeli activity nahi hai jisme Richards ke paas ek ajeeb intensity hai. Unka doosra pyaar cycling hai. Indeed, Dunedin, New Zealand mein ek shuruati tournament mein, woh kaam khatam hone ke baad apni bicycle par baithe, Christchurch se Dunedin tak poori raat paidal chalate (pedaled) rahe, jo pach sau miles (over two hundred miles) se zyaada ki distance thi, bina soye, aur subah sabse pehle tournament shuru kiya. Unke jeetne ke baad, tournament mein unse mile competitors ne unhein ghar tak ride offer ki. Unhone politely ise mana kar diya, Monday subah phir se kaam shuru karne se pehle ek aur bina-neend wali raat ke liye Christchurch ghar tak poore raaste wapas bicycle se jana prefer karte hue. Pehle toh unke profile mein yeh bas ek aur ajeeb anokha-pan (odd quirk) laga, jaise unke khud ke kiye gaye haircuts aur interview diye jaane ki anichha. Ab, halanki, mera vishwas hai ki yeh unke is mystery ko unlock karne ki kuch keys rakh sakta hai.

Cycling, beshak, koi badi mnemonic technique nahi hai. Agar yeh hoti, toh Lance Armstrong ek tivra pratiyogi (fierce contender) hote. Halanki, yeh Richards ki personality mein ek samanya theme ko pradarshit karta hai jo mere samna aaye doosre ultralearners ke sath overlap karti hai: ek aishi dhoon-bhari tivrata (obsessive intensity) jo prayas (effort) ke ek normal investment maane jaane wale se zyaada hoti hai. Richards ki cycling, it turns out, un akela doosre clues ke sath bhi achhi tarah line up karti hai jinhein main unke methods ke baare mein uncover karne kabil raha hoon: woh lists padhte hain; words ki lambi lists, do-letter words se shuru karke aur phir upar badhte hue. “Cycling madad karti hai,” woh explain karte hain, “Main apne mind mein lists ke beech se nikal sakta hoon.” Woh dictionary padhte hain, exclusively letters ke combinations par focus karte hue, definitions, tenses, aur plurals ko ignore karte hue. Phir, memory se draw karte hue, woh ghanton cycle chalate waqt unhein baar-baar repeat karte hain. Yeh aspect ek aise method se bhi mela khata hai jo doosre ultralearners mein samanya hai aur jo abhi tak learning ke doosre niyamon mein saamne aaya hai: **active recall aur rehearsal (dohrana)**. Words ko retrieve karke, Richards shayad apni pehle se hi impressive memory ko lete hain aur active practice ke zariye ise ajeedy/ajay (unassailable) bana dete hain.

Richards ki performance ke baare mein doosre clues hain: woh memory par focus karte hain, anagramming (words create karne liye tiles ko dobara arrange karna) par nahi; woh aage aur peeche kaam karte hain, chote words se shuru karke, bade walon par jaate hain aur wapas aate hain; woh claim karte hain ki words ko visually recall karte hain, kyunki jab words bole jaate hain toh woh unhein yaad nahi rakh sakte. Yeh saare clues Richards ke mind mein jhalak provide karte hain, lekin yeh jitna zahir karte hain usse kahin zyaada chhod dete hain. Unhein mentally rehearse karne kabil hone se pehle apni list se words ko kitni baar padhna padta hai? Kya words kisi tareeqe se organized hain ya bas alphabetically listed hain? Kya woh asadharn kshamtayon wale ek savant (viddhwan) hain jinki general intelligence normal se kam hai ya ek all-round genius hain jiske liye Scrabble words ko memorize karna unki kai impressive abilities mein se sirf ek hai? Shayad unki intelligence kaafi average hai aur Scrabble mein unka dabdaba (dominance) game ke prati unke charam samarpan (extreme dedication) ko represent karta hai. Hum shayad un sawaalon ke answers kabhi nahi jaan payenge.

Main nishchit roop se is theory ko kharij nahi kar sakta ki Richards ka mind simply meri apni memory ke mukable different tareeqe se ya behtar wired hai. Akhirkar, unke method ke baare mein abhi tak mere samna aayi koi bhi cheez itni boldly original nahi hai jisse serious Scrabble players anjaan hon. Phir bhi Richards ne apni competition par poori tarah se dominate kiya hai. Mera ek part suspect karta hai ki unki intense, obsessive personality, jo unhein ghanton cycle chalate hue mentally lists review karne kabil banati hai, shayad kam se kam ek partial explanation zoor banati hai. Unke paas jo bhi gifts hon, woh is book mein abhi tak mere dwara describe kiye gaye ultralearner ethos ko bhi apne paas rakhte lagte hain. Jo bhi iski keemat ho, Richards khud pehle ke mukable baad wale ke paksh mein mazeed tark dete hain: “Yeh hard work hai, aapko seekhne ke liye dedication rakhni hogi,” doosri jagah add karte hue “Main sure nahi hoon ki koi secret hai, yeh bas words ko seekhne ka mamla hai.”

Scrabble words aapki life ke liye important nahi ho sakte. Halanki, cheezon ko achhi tarah seekhne ke liye memory essential hai. Programmers ko apne code mein commands ke syntax ko yaad rakhna chahiye. Accountants ko ratios, rules, aur regulations ko memorize karne ki zarurat hoti hai. Lawyers ko precedents (purv-nazeer) aur statutes (kanoon) ko yaad rakhna chahiye. Doctors ko daso hazar factoids jaan'ne ki zarurat hoti hai, anatomical descriptions se lekar drug interactions tak. Memory essential hai, bhale hi yeh samajh (understanding), antardrishti (intuition), ya practical skill jaise bade ideas mein wrapped up ho. Koi cheez kaise kaam karti hai ya kisi khhas technique ko kaise perform karna hai ise samajhne kabil hona bematlab hai agar aap ise recall nahi kar sakte. Retention strategies ka upyog karne par depend karti hai taaki aap jo cheezein seekhte hain woh aapke mind se leak na hon. Retention ki strategies par discuss karne se pehle, halanki, aaiye is par ek nazar daalein ki cheezon ko yaad rakhna itna difficult kyun hai.

## Why Is It So Hard to Remember Things?

_(Cheezon Ko Yaad Rakhna Itna Mushkil Kyun Hai?)_

Richards ek extreme case hain, lekin unki kahani nevertheless (phir bhi) un saare themes ko pradarshit karti hai jo kisi ke liye bhi important hain jo kuch seekhna chahta hai: Aap un saari cheezon ko kaise retain kar sakte hain jinhein aap seekhte hain? Aap hard-won facts aur skills ko bhoolne (forgetting) ke khilaf kaise defend kar sakte hain? Aapne jo knowledge acquire ki hai use kaise store kar sakte hain taaki jab aapko zarurat ho tab ise exactly aasaani se retrieved kiya ja sake? Learning ko samajhne liye, aapko yeh samajhne ki zarurat hai ki aap kaise aur kyun bhoolte hain.

Pehle seekhi gayi jankari tak access khona educators, students, aur psychologists ke liye ek sada-bahaar (perennial) problem rahi hai. Dhundhli hoti knowledge (fading knowledge) aapke dwara kiye jaane wale kaam par bhi impact daalati hai. Ek study ne report kiya ki doctors jitna lamba kaam karte hain, woh utna hi badtar medical care dete hain, kyunki medical school se unki stored knowledge gradually bhooli jaati hai, field mein full-time kaam karne ke bavajood. Original abstract se quote karte hue:

> Zyaada experience wale physicians ke baare mein aam taur par maana jata hai ki unhone abhyas ke saalon mein knowledge aur skills ikhatha ki hain aur isliye woh high-quality care deliver karte hain. Halanki, evidence suggest karta hai ki ek physician ke abhyas mein rahe saalon ki sankhya aur us physician dwara provide ki jaane wali care ki quality ke beech ek ulta rishta (inverse relationship) hota hai.

Hermann Ebbinghaus ne, history ke pehle psychological experiments mein se ek mein, saalon bematlab ke sabd-khando (nonsense syllables) ko memorize karne mein bitaye, theek usi tareeqe se jaise Richards Scrabble words memorize karte hain, aur baad mein unhein recall karne ki apni ability ko saavdhani se track kiya. Is original research se, jise baad mein mazeed prayogatmak roop se mazboot studies (experimentally robust studies) dwara verify kiya gaya, Ebbinghaus ne **forgetting curve (bismriti vakra)** ko discover kiya.

Yeh curve dikhata hai ki hum cheezon ko seekhne ke baad hairatangez roop se tezi se bhoolne ki taraf jhukte hain, jankari mein ek ghaatank kshay (exponential decay in knowledge) hota hai, jo seekhne ke theek baad sabse zyaada teez (steepest) hota hai. Halanki, Ebbinghaus ne note kiya, yeh bhoolna kam ho jata hai (tapers off), aur bhooli jaane wali jankari ki matra samay ke sath kam ho jaati hai. Hamara mind ek tooti hui balti (leaky bucket) hai; halanki, zyaada tar holes top ke paas hain, isliye jo pani bottom par bacha rehta hai woh mazeed slowly leak hota hai.

In intervening saalon mein, psychologists ne kam se kam teen dominant theories ko identify kiya hai taaki yeh explain karne mein madad mil sake ki hamare brains shuruat mein seekhe gaye hisse ka zyaada tar hissa kyun bhool jaate hain: **decay, interference, aur forgotten cues.** Bhale hi juri abhi bhi insani long-term memory ke peeche ke exact mechanism par baahar hai, yeh teen ideas nishchit roop se is baat ko explain karne ka kuch hissa banate hain ki hum cheezon ko kyun bhoolte hain aur, iske ulat, is baare mein insight provide karte hain ki hum jo seekhte hain use behtar kaise retain kar sakte hain.

### 1. Decay: Forgetting with Time

_(Kshay: Samay Ke Sath Bhoolna)_
Bhoolne ka pehla theory yeh hai ki memories simply samay ke sath decay (kshay) ho jaati hain. Yeh idea common sense se match karta lagta hai. Hum pichle hafte seekhi gayi events, news, aur cheezon ko pichle mahine ki cheezon ke mukable kahin zyaada saaf yaad rakhte hain. Is saal seekhi gayi cheezon ko ek dashak pehle ki events ke mukable kahin zyaada accuracy ke sath recall kiya jata hai. Is samajh ke tehat, bhoolna simply samay dwara ek apariharya ksharan (inevitable erosion by time) hai. Ek hourglass mein rait ki tarah, hamari memories nishthur roop se humse door phisal jaati hain jaise-jaise hum unse mazeed door hote jaate hain.

Halanki is theory ke poora explanation hone ke sath dararein (flaws) hain. Hum mein se kai log bachpan ke shuruati events ko vividly recall kar sakte hain, bhale hi hamein yaad na ho ki humne pichle Tuesday ko breakfast mein kya khaya tha. Aise patterns bhi lagte hain jisme kaun si cheezein yaad rakkhi jaati hain aur kaun si bhooli jaati hain jo unke originally seekhe jaane ke samay se pare jaati hain: saaf, arthpurna (vivid, meaningful) cheezon ko mamuli ya manmaani jankariyon (banal or arbitrary information) ke mukable mazeed aasaani se recall kiya jata hai. Bhale hi hamare bhoolne mein ek component ho jo simply decay hai, yeh tezi se asambhavit (unlikely) lagta hai ki yahi akela factor hai.

### 2. Interference: Overwriting Old Memories with New Ones

_(Hastakshep: Purani Memories Ke Upar Nayi Memories Likhna)_
Interference ek different idea suggest karta hai: ki hamari memories, ek computer ki files ke ulat, brain mein unke store hone ke tareeqe mein ek doosre ke upar overlap karti hain. Is tareeqe se, jo memories similar hain lekin distinct hain woh ek doosre ke sath compete kar sakti hain. Agar aap programming seekh rahe hain, for instance, aap seekh sakte hain ki ek _for loop_ kya hai aur ise kisi cheez ko baar-baar karne ke mamle mein yaad rakh sakte hain. Baad mein, aap _while loops, recursion, repeat-until loops, aur go-to statements_ ke baare mein seekh sakte hain. Ab, inmein se har ek ka talluk kisi cheez ko baar-baar karne se hai, lekin different tareeqon se, isliye woh is baare mein correctly yaad karne ki aapki ability ke sath interfere kar sakte hain ki ek for loop kya karta hai.

Iske kam se kam do flavors hain: **proactive interference** aur **retroactive interference**.

- **Proactive interference** tab hota hai jab pehle seekhi gayi jankari nayi jankari haasil karne ko harder banati hai. Ise aise sochein jaise woh “space” jahan us jankari ko store kiya jana hai pehle se hi occupied (ghira hua) hai, isliye nayi memory banana harder ho jata hai. Yeh tab ho sakta hai jab aap kisi word ka definition seekhna chahte hain lekin difficulty hoti hai kyunki us word ka pehle se hi aapke mind mein ek different association hai. Psychology mein _negative reinforcement_ ke concept ko seekhne ki koshish par vichar karne—yahan “negative” word ka matlab “absent” (gair-majood) hai, bajaye “bad” (kharab) ke, isliye negative reinforcement tab hota hai jab aap kisi cheez ko hata kar, maan lijiye ek painful stimulus ko, kisi behaviour ke liye encourage karte hain. Halanki, chunki negative ka “bad” wala pehle ka matlab pehle se exist karta hai, aapko ise yaad rakhne mein difficulty ho sakti hai aur negative reinforcement ko punishment ke barabar galat man'na aasan ho jata hai.
- **Retroactive interference** iska ulta hai—jahan kuch naya seekhna ek purani memory ko “erase” (mita) ya suppress kar deta hai. Jo bhi Spanish seekh chuka hai aur baad mein French seekhne ki koshish ki hai woh jaanta hai ki retroactive interference kitna pechida ho sakta hai, jab aap phir se Spanish bolna chahte hain toh French words baahar nikalte (pop out) hain.

### 3. Forgotten Cues: A Locked Box with No Key

_(Bhoolay Gaye Ishare: Ek Band Box Bina Kisi Key Ke)_
Bhoolne ka teesra theory kehta hai ki hamari paas majood kai memories actually bhooli nahi jaati hain balki simply agammye/pahunch se baahar (inaccessible) hoti hain. Idea yahan yeh hai ki yeh kehne ke liye ki kisi ne koi cheez yaad rakkhi hai, use memory se retrieved karne ki zarurat hoti hai. Chunki hum apni long-term memories ke poore hisse ko same samay par lagaatar experience nahi kar rahe hote hain, iska matlab hai ki ek sahi cue diye jaane par jankari ko ugalwane (dredging up) ki koi process honi chahiye. Us case mein jo ho sakta hai woh yeh hai ki jankari ko retrieve karne ki chain ke links mein se ek toot (severed) gaya hai (shayad decay ya interference dwara) aur isliye poori memory inaccessible ho gayi hai. Halanki, agar us cue ko restore kar diya jaye, ya agar jankari tak pahunche ka koi alternate path dhoondha ja sake, toh hum usse kahin zyaada yaad rakhenge jo currently hamari pahunch mein hai.

Yeh explanation ke paas bhi kuch advantages hain. Sahaj roop se (Intuitively) yeh kuch had tak sach lagta hai, kyunki hum sab tongue-of-the-tip (baat zubaan par hona) ke experience ko jaantee hain, jab hum aisa feel karte hain jaise hamein koi fact ya word yaad rakhne kabil hona chahiye lekin hum ise immediately summon up nahi kar sakte. Yeh yeh bhi suggest kar sakta hai ki cheezon ko dobara seekhna (relearning) unhein shuruat mein seekhne ke mukable kahin zyaada tez hai, kyunki relearning marammat ke kaam (repair work) ke mazeed paas hai, jabki original learning poori tarah se ek nayi construction hai. Cues ka bhoolna saari cheezon ko bhoolne ke ek partial, agar complete nahi toh, explanation ke roop mein highly likely lagta hai.

Mnemonic chintao ke liye ek complete explanation ke roop mein cue ka bhoolna, halanki, problems ke bina nahi hai. Kai memory researchers ab vishwas karte hain ki yaad rakhne ka act koi nishkriya process (passive process) nahi hai. Facts, events, ya jankariyon ko recall karne mein, hum punarnirman ki ek ranatmak process (creative process of reconstruction) mein engage ho rahe hain. Memories khud aksar yaad rakhne ki process mein modified, enhanced, ya manipulated ho jaati hain. Yeh ho sakta hai, phir, ki “lost” memories jinhein naye cues ke zariye retrieved kiya jata hai woh actually fabrications (gaddhi hui baatein) hon. Yeh traumatic events se “recovered” witness testimony ke case mein khhasakar likely lagta hai, kyunki experiments ne dikhaya hai ki bhale hi highly saaf memories jo subject ko poori tarah se authentic feel hoti hain woh asatya (untrue) ho sakti hain.

## How Can You Prevent Forgetting?

_(Aap Bhoolne Ko Kaise Rok Sakte Hain?)_

Bhoolna default hai, exception nahi, isliye mere samna aaye ultralearners ne life ke is fact se cope karne ke liye tarah-tarah ki strategies taiyar ki thin. Yeh methods do similar lekin different problems se nipatne mein mota-mota divide hote hain.

- **Methods ka pehla set ultralearning project ko anjam dete waqt retention ki problem se deal karta hai:** Aap pehle hafte seekhi gayi cheezon ko kaise retain kar sakte hain, taaki aapko aakhiri hafte tak unhein dobara seekhne ki zarurat na pade? Yeh Benny Lewis ki language learning aur Roger Craig ki Jeopardy! trivia mastery jaise memory-intensive ultralearning prayason ke liye khhasakar important hai. In domains aur kai doosron mein, seekhi jaane wali jankari ka volume aksar itna bada hota hai ki bhoolna vyavaharik roop se lagbhag immediately ek badha (practical obstacle) ban jata hai.
- **Methods ka doosra set, iske ulat, project ke complete hone ke baad acquired skills aur knowledge ki deerghayu (longevity) se talluk rakhta hai:** Ek baar jab ek bhasha ko ek aise level tak seekh liya gaya hai jisse aap satisfied hain, toh aap khud ko ek-do saal baad ise poori tarah se bhoolne se kaise rok sakte hain?

Mere samna aaye ultralearners ne in do problems se nipatne ke liye alag-alag methods taiyar kiye the, jo effort aur intensity mein vary karte the. Dave Craig ki tarah, kuch ne jatil electronic systems (elaborate electronic systems) ko prefer kiya jo fancy algorithms ke sath memory ko optimize kar sakein, jisme kam waste aur inefficiency bachti hai, bhale hi iski keemat mazeed complexity lana ho. Nigel Richards ki tarah, doosre un basic systems ko prefer karte lagte hain jo apni simplicity par succeed hote hain.

Aapko ek aisi mnemonic system chun'ne ki zarurat hai, jo aapke goals ko bhi accomplish kare aur tike rehne ke liye kafi simple ho. Language learning ke tivra periods ke dauran, vocabulary ke vishhal volume ka matlab aksar mere liye spaced-repetition systems ka sahayak hona tha. Doosre samay, maine bolne ki apni ability ko maintain karne ke liye conversations karne ko prefer kiya, bhale hi yeh method kaafi sateek (precise) na ho. Doosre subjects ke sath, main bhoolne ke kuch darje tak ke liye allow karne mein mazeed khush hoon jab tak ki main un skills ki practice karta hoon jinhein mujhe lagaatar use karne ki zarurat hai aur dobara seekhne (relearn) ki ability rakhta hoon.

Mere approaches bhale hi ek theoretical ideal tak na pahunche, lekin woh aakhirkar behtar kaam kar sakte hain kyunki unke paas error ke liye kam possibilities hain aur unhein mazeed aasaani se sustain kiya ja sakta hai. Gair-zaruri roop se use kiye gaye exact system se pare, halanki, saare systems char mechanisms mein se ek ke mutabik kaam karte dikhte hain: **spacing, proceduralization, overlearning, ya mnemonics.** Aaiye pehle retention ke in saare mechanisms ko dekhein, taaki different ultralearning projects mein use kiye jaane wale kaafi different aur idiosyncrasic pradarshano ko samajh (make sense) saken.

### Memory Mechanism 1 — Spacing: Repeat to Remember

_(Retention Ka Tarika 1 — Spacing: Yaad Rakhne Ke Liye Dohraein)_
Studying advice ke un pieces mein se ek jise research dwara sabse behtar samarthan (backed) mila hai woh yeh hai ki agar aap long-term retention ke baare mein care karte hain, toh **cram (ratta/ek sath thosna) mat karein.** Samay ke mazeed intervals par lambe periods mein learning sessions ko phailana short run mein thoda kamzor performance ka kaaran banta hai (kyunki intervals ke beech bhoolne ka ek chance hota hai) lekin long run mein kahin zyaada behtar performance deta hai. Yeh ek aisi cheez thi jiske baare mein mujhe MIT Challenge ke dauran saavdhaan rehne ki zarurat thi. Meri pehli kuch classes ke baad, maine ek baar mein ek class karne se badalkar parallel mein kuch classes karne par switch kiya, taaki rammed study samay ka meri memory par padne wale impact ko kam (minimize) kiya ja sake.

Agar aapke paas kisi cheez ko seekhne ke liye das ghante hain, isliye, ek burst mein das ghante study karne ke bajaye das din har din ek ghante study karne mein spend karna kahin zyaada sense banata hai. Obviously, halanki, agar study intervals ke beech ka samay lamba aur lamba hota jata hai, toh short-term effects long-term waale par bhaari padne lagte hain. Agar aap study intervals ke beech ek dashak ke batware ke sath kuch seekhte hain, toh yeh kaafi possible hai ki aap doosre session tak pahunchna se pehle pehle seekhi gayi har cheez ko poori tarah se bhool jayenge.

Bahut lamba aur bahut chhote ke beech ka exact trade-off point dhoondhna kuch ultralearners ke liye ek chhota dhun (minor obsession) raha hai. Apne study sessions ko bahut zyaada paas space karein, aur aap efficiency kho dete hain; unhein bahut zyaada door space karein, aur aap pehle se seekhi gayi cheez ko bhool jaate hain. Isne kai ultralearners ko kam se kam effort ke sath zyaada tar jankari ko retain karne ke ek tool ke roop mein **spaced-repetition systems (SRS)** apply karne par dhakela hai. Roger Craig ki Jeopardy! trivia memorization ke peeche SRS ek mukhya force thi, aur maine Chinese aur Korean seekhte waqt in systems ka vyapak roop se upyog kiya. Bhale hi aapne yeh shabd na suna ho, yeh general niyan kai language-learning products ka backbone hai, jisme Pimsleur, Memrise, aur Duolingo shamil hain. Yeh programs spacing algorithm ko background mein chhupane ki taraf jhukte hain, isliye aapko iske sath khud ko takleef dene ki zarurat nahi hoti. Halanki, doosre programs, jaise open-source _Anki_, un zyaada extreme ultralearners ke preferred tool hain jo thoda mazeed performance nikaalna (squeeze out) chahte hain.

SRS ek adbhut tool hai, lekin yeh kaafi focused applications rakhne ki taraf jhukta hai. Facts, trivia, vocabulary words, ya definitions seekhna flash card software ke liye ideally suited hai, jo jankari ko ek single answer wale sawaal ke roop mein prastut karta hai. Jankari ke mazeed complicated domains par ise apply karna harder hai, jo jankariyon ke complex associations par nirbhar karte hain jinhein kevel real-world practice ke zariye hi build kiya jata hai. Phir bhi, kuch tasks ke liye, memory ka bottleneck itna tang hota hai ki SRS ise chouda karne ke liye ek powerful tool hai, bhale hi iske kuch drawbacks hon. Medical students ke liye ek popular study guide ke authors apne approach ko SRS ke chaaron taraf center karte hain, kyunki ek medical student ko bahut si cheezein yaad rakhni hoti hain aur bhoolne aur dobara seekhne ki default strategy samay ke mamle mein kaafi costly hoti hai.

Spacing ke liye complex software ki zarurat nahi hoti, halanki. Jaisa ki Richards ki kahani saaf pradarshit karti hai, simply words ki lists print karna, unhein padhna, aur phir unhein samne rakkhe bina mentally rehearse karna ek incredibly powerful technique hai. Similarly, kisi skill ka semiregular abhyas aksar kaafi sahayak hota hai. Bhashon ko seekhne ke apne saal ke baad, main yeh ensure karna chahta tha ki main unhein bhooloon nahi. Mera approach kaafi simple tha: week mein ek baar thirty minutes ka conversation practice schedule karna, jise Skype ke zariye _italki_ ka use karke kiya jaye, jo duniya bhar mein tutoring aur language exchange partners ke liye ek online service hai. Maine ise ek saal tak maintain kiya, jiske baad main agle do saalon ke liye per-month ek baar ki practice par drops ho gaya. Main nahi jaanta ki yeh practice schedule ideal tha ya nahi, aur mere paas practice karne ke doosre opportunities bhi the jo us samay ke dauran sahaj roop se saamne aaye jinhone madad bhi ki, lekin mera vishwas hai ki yeh kuch na karne aur skills ko kamzor (atrophy) hone dene se kahin behtar tha. Jab retention ki baat aati hai, toh **perfect ko good enough (kafi achha) ka dushman mat banne dein.**

Spacing apply karne ki ek aur strategy, jo un mazeed elaborate skills ke liye behtar kaam kar सकती hai jinhein aapki daily habits mein integrate karna harder hota hai, semiregular roop se **refresher projects** karna hai. Maine MIT Challenge ke dauran seekhi gayi cheezon ke liye is approach ka sahara liya, kyunki jis skill ko main sabse zyaada retain karna chahta tha woh code likhna tha, jise per week sirf ek aadhe ghante par karna pechida hai. Is approach ka disadvantage kabhi-kabhi optimal spacing se kaafi deviate (bhatakna) hona hai; halanki, agar aap compensate karne ke liye thoda sa relearning karne ke liye prepared hain, toh yeh practice ko poori tarah se chhod dene se abhi bhi ek behtar approach ho sakti hai. Is tarah ke maintenance ko pehle se schedule karna bhi sahayak ho sakta hai, kyunki yeh aapko yaad dilayega ki learning koi aishi cheez nahi hai jise ek baar kiya gya aur phir ignore kar diya gaya balki ek aishi process hai jo aapki poori life chalti rehti hai.

### Memory Mechanism 2 — Proceduralization: Automatic Will Endure

_(Retention Ka Tarika 2 — Proceduralization: Automatic Cheezein Tikengi)_
Log kyun kehte hain ki yeh “bicycle chalane jaisa” hai aur “trigonometry yaad rakhne jaisa” nahi? Yeh common expression pehli jagah dikhne ke mukable mazeed gehri neurological realities mein rooted ho sakta hai. Is baat ke evidences hain ki procedural skills (prakriyatmak hunar), jaise bicycle chalana, declarative knowledge (bayanatmak gyan), jaise Pythagorean Theorem ya triangles ke liye Sine Rule jaan'ne ke mukable ek different tareeqe se store hoti hain. _Knowing how_ (kaise karna hai jaan'ne) aur _knowing that_ (kya hai jaan'ne) ke beech ka yeh farq long-term memory ke liye different prabhav rakh sakta hai. Procedural skills, jaise hamesha-yaad-rehne-wali bicycling, bhoolay jaane ke prati us knowledge ke mukable kahin kam su-grahya (susceptible) hoti hain jise retrieve karne ke liye explicit recall ki zarurat hoti hai.

Is finding ka use actually hamare advantage ke liye kiya ja sakta hai. Learning ke ek dominant theory suggest karta hai ki zyaada tar skills stages se guzarti hain—declarative se shuru hokar lekin jaise-jaise aap mazeed practice karte hain procedural par ant hoti hain. Is declarative-to-procedural transition ka ek perfect example **typewriting** hai. Jab aap keyboard par typing shuru karte hain, toh aapko letters ki positions ko memorize karna hota hai. Har baar jab aap koi word type karna chahte hain, toh aapko iske letters ke mamle mein sochna padta hai, keyboard par har ek ki position ko recall karna padta hai, aur phir press karne ke liye apni finger ko us spot par move karna padta hai. Yeh process fail ho sakti hai; aap bhool sakte hain ki ek key kahan hai aur ise type karne ke liye neeche dekhne ki zarurat pad sakti hai.

Halanki, agar aap mazeed abhyas karte hain, toh aap neeche dekhna band kar dete hain. Aakhirkar aap letters ki positions ya unse milne ke liye apni fingers ko move karne ke baare mein sochna band kar dete hain. Aap yahan tak ki ek aise point par pahunch sakte hain jahan aap letters ke baare mein bilkul nahi sochte aur ek baar mein poore words baahar nikalte hain. Aishi procedural knowledge kaafi robust (mazboot) hoti hai aur declarative knowledge ke mukable kahin zyaada lamba retain hone ki taraf jhukti hai. Ek quick observation ise verify karne liye kafi hai: jab aap typing mein sach mein achhe ho gaye hon aur koi aapise quickly kehne ke liye kahe ki keyboard par letter _w_ kahan hai, toh aapko sahi tarah se batane ke liye actually apne haathon ko keyboard ki position mein rakhna pad sakta hai (ya imagine karna pad sakta hai ki aap aisa kar rahe hain) aur pretend to type karna pad sakta hai. Theek wahi mere sath hua jab main is paragraph ko type kar raha tha. Jo hua hai woh yeh hai ki jo originally jankari tak primary access point tha, key location ki aapki explicit memory, woh fade away ho gayi hai aur ab use aapke motor movements mein encoded mazeed durable procedural knowledge ke sath recall karne ki zarurat hai. Agar aapko kabhi koi password ya pin code enter karna pada hai jise aap aksar use karte hain, toh aap ek similar position mein ho sakte hain, jahan aap ise feel se yaad rakhte hain na ki iske numbers aur letters ke explicit combination se.

Is fact ke kaaran ki procedural jankari mazeed lambe samay tak store rehti hai, yeh ek useful heuristic (khoj-niyan) suggest kar sakta hai. Jankari ya skills ke ek bade volume ko evenly seekhne ke bajaye, aap information ke ek core set ko kahin zyaada frequently highlight (emphasize) kar sakte hain, taaki yeh procedural ban jaye aur kahin zyaada lamba store rahe. Yeh mere dost aur mere bhasha-seekhne ke project ka ek anjaane mein side effect tha. Ek bhasha lagaatar bolne par majboor hone ka matlab tha ki phrases aur patterns ke ek core set ko itni baar repeat kiya gaya ki hum mein se koi bhi unhein kabhi nahi bhoolega. Yeh kam frequently use hone wale dheron words ya phrases ke liye sach nahi ho sakta, lekin conversations ke starting points ko yaad rakhna lagbhag impossible hai. Language studies ka classic approach, jisme students beginner words aur grammatical patterns se mazeed complicated waale par “move on” kar jaate hain, shayad isse bach nikalta hai, taaki woh core patterns repeated practice ke bina saalon tak tikne ke liye kaafi sticky na hon.

Core skills ko fully proceduralize karne mein fail hona mere pehle bade swa-shiksha prayas, MIT Challenge ki ek mukhya khami (major flaw) thi, jise main apne baad ke bhasha-seekhne aur portrait-drawing projects mein behtar banane kabil raha. Gair-zaruri roop se MIT Challenge mein core mathematical aur programming skills thin jinhein aksar repeat kiya jata tha, jo aakhirkar proceduralized hua woh mazeed haphazard tha bajaye computer science apply karne ke sabse essential skills ko automate karne ke ek sachet faisala (conscious decision) ko represent karne ke.

Zyaada tar skills jinhein hum seekhte hain woh incompletely proceduralized hoti hain. Hum unmein se kuch ko automatically karne kabil ho sakte hain, lekin doosre parts ke liye hamein apne minds ko active roop se search karne ki zarurat hoti hai. Aap, for instance, algebra mein equation ke ek side se doosri side variables ko bina soche aasaani se move karne kabil ho sakte hain. Lekin jab exponents ya trigonometry shamil hoti hai toh aapko thoda mazeed sochna pad sakta hai. Shayad, unqi nature ke kaaran, kuch skills ko poori tarah se automate nahi kiya ja sakta aur unhein hamesha kuch sachet soch (conscious thought) ki zarurat hogi. Yeh knowledge ka ek interesting mix create karta hai, jisme kuch cheezein lambe periods mein kaafi stably retain rehti hain aur doosri bhoolay jaane ke prati su-grahya (susceptible) hoti hain.

Is concept ko apply karne ki ek strategy practice khatam hone se pehle ek nirdharit matra mein knowledge ko poori tarah se proceduralized karna ensure karna ho sakti hai. Ek aur approach kuch skills ko proceduralize karne ke liye extra effort spend karna ho sakti hai, jo doosri jankariyon ke liye cues ya access points ke roop mein kaam karengi. Aap kisi naye programming project par kaam shuru karne ke liye use ki jaane wali process ko poori tarah se proceduralize karne ka maqsad rakh sakte hain, for example, taaki aap naya program likhne ki process mein us hump (badha) ko paar kar sakein. Yeh strategies thodi speculative (anumanit) hain, lekin main socha hoon ki dimaag ke declarative-to-procedural transition ko future mein chalaak ultralearners dwara apply kiye jaane ke kai potential tareeqe hain.

### Memory Mechanism 3 — Overlearning: Practice Beyond Perfect

_(Retention Ka Tarika 3 — Overlearning: Perfect Se Pare Abhyas)_
Overlearning ek achhi tarah studied psychological phenomenon hai jise samajhna kaafi aasan hai: **adequate (paryapt) perform karne ke liye jitni required hai usse pare additional practice, un periods ki length ko badha sakti hai jisme memories store rehti hain.** Typical experimental setup subjects ko ek task dena hai, jaise ek rifle ko assemble karna ya kisi emergency checklist se guzarna, unhein practice karne ke liye kaafi samay dena taaki woh ise ek baar correctly kar sakein. Zero se is point tak ka samay “learning” phase maana jata hai. Next, subjects ko “overlearning” ki different matraon (amounts) ke liye allow karein, yaani practice jo pehli correct application ke baad bhi jaari rehti hai. Chunki subjects pehle se hi skill correctly kar rahe hain, performance is point se aage behtar nahi hoti. Halanki, overlearning skill ki durability ko badha sakti hai.

Uss typical setting mein jisme overlearning ka study kiya gaya hai, overlearning ke asaron ki duration kaafi chhoti hoti hai; ek session mein thoda lamba abhyas karna recall ke ek ya do extra weeks produce karta hai. Yeh imply kar sakta hai ki overlearning mukhya roop se ek short-term phenomenon hai: first aid ya emergency response protocols jaise skills ke liye kuch useful, jinqi practice rarely hoti hai lekin niyamit training sessions ke beech unhein fresh rakhne ki zarurat hoti hai. Main suspect karta hoon, halanki, ki overlearning ke paas mazeed long-term implications ho sakte hain agar ise much longer projects par spacing aur proceduralization ke sath combine kiya jaye. Portraits draw karne ke mere apne personal experience mein, for instance, Vitruvian Studio se seekhe gaye facial features ko map karne ke liye use ki jaane wali thought process itni baar repeat hui thi ki ise bhoolna hard hai, bhale hi mera mukhya practice samay sirf ek mahine ke dauran tha. Similarly, programming ya mathematics ke khhas reflexes ko main abhi bhi apne MIT Challenge ke dino se aasaani se recall kar sakta hoon, beech ke samay mein practice ke bina bhi, kyunki woh aise chuninda patterns the jinhein us samay adequately perform karne ke liye jitna zaroori tha usse kahin zyaada baar repeat kiya gaya tha (kyunki woh mazeed elaborate problems ke ghaatak the).

Overlearning directness ke niyan ke sath achhi tarah dovetails (mel khati) hai. Kyunki kisi skill ka direct use frequently khhas core abilities ki overpracticing ko shamil karta hai, woh kernel aam taur par bhoolne ke prati kaafi resistant hota hai, saalon baad bhi. Iske ulat, academically seekhe gaye subjects practice ko mazeed evenly distribute karne ki taraf jhukte hain taaki har ek area mein competency ke ek minimum level tak poore curriculum ko cover kiya ja sake, bina practical applications ke subtopics ke kendriyata (centrality) ke. Saalon ki formal schooling ke zariye bhasha seekhne wale logon ke paas mere mukable grammatical nuances ka kahin zyaada impressive vocabularies ya knowledge hota hai. Halanki, wahi log kaafi basic phrases par ladkhada (trip over) sakte hain, kyunki unhone har ek fact aur skill ko evenly seekha, bajaye tezi se samanya patterns ke chhote subset ko overlearning karne ke.

Aise do mukhya tareeqe lagte hain jinse mera samna overlearning apply karne ke liye hua hai.

- **Pehla core practice hai,** kisi skill ke core elements ki lagaatar practice aur refinement karna. Yeh approach aksar shuruati ultralearning phase complete hone ke baad, kisi tarah ke immersion ya vyapak projects (vyapak roop se, tivra roop se nahi) par kaam karne ke sath achha pair banta hai. Shuruat mein seekhne se lekar yahan karne tak ka shift actually learning ke ek mazeed gehre, mazeed baareek roop ko shamil kar sakta hai, jise simply pehle seekhi gayi knowledge apply karne ke roop mein discount nahi kiya jana chahiye.
- **Doosri strategy advanced practice hai,** skills ke ek nirdharit set se ek level upar jana taaki lower-level skills ke core parts overlearned ho sakein jaise koi unhein ek mazeed difficult domain mein apply karta hai. Algebra ke students ke ek study ne is doosri strategy ko pradarshit kiya. Zyaada tar students jinhone ek algebra class li thi aur saalon baad unka dobara test liya gaya tha woh jo seekha tha uska ek vishal hissa bhool chuke the. Yeh ya toh isliye ho sakta tha kyunki jankari sahi mayne mein lost ho gayi thi ya simply isliye kyunki forgotten cues ne iske zyaada tar hisse ko inaccessible bana diya tha. Interestingly, bhale hi behtar aur kharab perform karne wale students ke liye bhoolne ki yeh rate same thi; behtar students ne kamzor walon ke mukable zyaada retain rakkha, lekin jis raftaar se woh bhoole the woh same thi. Ek group ne, halanki, bhoolne mein aishi teez giravat nahi dikhai: **jinhone calculus li thi.** Yeh suggest karta hai ki ek mazeed advanced skill ke liye ek level upar badhne ne pehle ki skill ko overlearned hone kabil banaya, is tarah kuch bhoolne ko roka.

### Memory Mechanism 4 — Mnemonics: A Picture Retains a Thousand Words

_(Retention Ka Tarika 4 — Mnemonics: Ek Chitr Ek Hazar Shabdon Ko Tikata Hai)_
Mere samna aaye kai ultralearners ke liye samanya aakhiri tool mnemonics tha. Kai mnemonic strategies hain, aur un saari ko cover karna is book ke scope se baahar hai. Unmein jo cheez sanjha hai woh yeh hai ki woh hyperspecific (behad vishisht) hone ki taraf jhukti hain—yaani, unhein jankari ke bahut hi vishisht patterns (very specific patterns of information) ko yaad rakhne liye design kiya jata hai. Doosre, unme aam taur par amurt ya manmaani jankariyon (abstract or arbitrary information) ko saaf chitron (vivid pictures) ya spatial maps mein translate karna shamil hota hai.

Jab mnemonics kaam karti hain, toh results par vishwas karna lagbhag difficult ho sakta hai. Mathematical constant pi ke digits ko memorize karne ke liye Guinness World Record holder, Rajveer Meena, number ko 70,000 decimal places tak jaante hain. Master mnemonicists, jo memory ke championships mein compete karte hain, sixty seconds se kam mein cards ke ek deck ke order ko memorize kar sakte hain aur adhyayan karne ke sirf ek ya do minutes baad ek poem ko verbatim (shabdshah) repeat kar sakte hain. Yeh carname kaafi impressive hain, aur isse bhi behtar, inhein koi bhi seekh sakta hai jo unhein apply karne ke liye kaafi patient ho. Woh kaise kaam karte hain?

Ek common, aur useful, mnemonic ko **keyword method** ke roop mein jaana jata hai. Yeh method pehle ek foreign-language word ko lekar aur use apni native bhasha mein kisi aishi cheez mein convert karke kaam karta hai jaisa yeh sunne mein lagta hai. Agar main aisa French ke sath kar raha tha, for example, main word _chavirer_ (to capsize - palatna) le sakta hoon aur ise “shave an ear” (ek kaan mundna) mein convert kar sakta hoon, jiske sound mein yeh itna paas hai ki baad wala original word ko recall karne ke liye ek effective cue ke roop mein kaam karega. Next main ek mental image create karta hoon jo foreign word ke sounds-like version aur ek ajeeb aur saaf setting mein iske translation ke ek chitr ko combine karti hai jo bizarre aur bhoolne mein hard ho. Is case mein, main ek vishal kaan (giant ear) ki kalpana kar sakta hoon jo ek boat mein baith kar apni lambi daadhi shave kar raha hai jo boat chavirer (capsizes) ho jaati hai. Phir, jab bhi mujhe yaad karne ki zarurat hoti hai ki French mein “capsize” kya hai, main capsizing ke baare mein sochta hoon, apni us bani hui picture ko recall karta hoon, jo “shaving an ear” se link karti hai aur is tarah . . . _chavirer_.

Yeh process shuruat mein fuzool mein jatil aur vistar-bhhari (needlessly complicated and elaborate) lagti hai, lekin yeh ek difficult association (arbitrary sounds aur ek naye matlab ke beech) ko kuch aise links mein convert karne se benefit leti hai jinhein associate aur yaad rakhna kahin zyaada aasan hota hai. Practice ke sath, is tarah ka har ek conversion sirf fifteen se twenty seconds le sakta hai, aur yeh foreign-language words ko yaad rakhne mein sach mein madad karta hai. Yeh particular tarah ki mnemonic is maqsad ke liye kaam karti hai, lekin doosri hain jo lists, numbers, maps, ya kisi procedure mein steps ke sequences ko yaad rakhne liye kaam karti hain. Is topic par ek achhe introduction ke liye, main Joshua Foer ki kitab _Moonwalking with Einstein: The Art and Science of Remembering Everything_ ki high recommendation karta hoon.

Mnemonics achha kaam karti hain, aur practice ke sath, koi bhi unhein kar sakta hai. Kyun, phir, woh is chapter mein peeche ke bajaye mukhya roop se front aur center mein nahi hain? Mera vishwas hai ki mnemonics, SRS ki tarah, incredibly powerful tools hain. Aur tools ke roop mein, woh un logon ke liye nayi possibilities khol sakte hain jo unse familiar nahi hain. Halanki, kisi aise insaan ke roop mein jisne unhein explore karne aur unhein real-world learning par apply karne mein bahut saara samay bitaya hai, unke applications pehle dikhne ke mukable kaafi had tak narrow (tang) hain, aur kai real-world settings mein woh simply pareshani (hassle) ke layak nahi hain.

Mera vishwas hai ki mnemonics ke do disadvantages hain.

- **Pehla yeh hai ki sabse impressive mnemonics systems** (jaise mathematical constant pi ke hazaron digits ko memorize karne wala), unhein pehle se hi ek mahatvapurna up-front investment ki zarurat hoti hai. Aapke khatam karne ke baad, aap digits ko aasaani se memorize kar sakte hain, lekin yeh actually koi bahut zyaada useful task nahi hai. Hamari zyaada tar samaj is fact ke chaaron taraf adapt hoti hai ki log aam taur par digits ko memorize nahi kar sakte, isliye hamare paas aisa karne ke liye paper aur computers hain.
- **Doosra disadvantage yeh hai ki mnemonics se recall karna** aksar directly kisi cheez ko yaad rakhne jitna automatic nahi hota. Kisi foreign-language word ke liye ek mnemonic jaan'ne se behtar hai ki aap use poori tarah se yaad karne mein fail ho jayein, lekin yeh abhi bhi aapko mnemonically yaad rakkhe gaye words se faraatedar sentences form karne ki izazat dene ke liye bahut slow hai. Is tarah mnemonics yaad rakhne mein difficult jankari ke liye ek bridge (pull) ke roop mein kaam kar sakte hain, lekin yeh aam taur par hamesha ke liye tikne wali memories create karne mein final step nahi hota.

Mnemonics, isliye, ek incredibly powerful agar thodi bhangur (brittle) tool hain. Agar aap koi aisa task kar rahe hain jisme ek bahut hi vishisht format mein highly dense jankari ko memorize karne ki zarurat hai, khhasakar agar jankari ka use kuch hafte ya mahino ke dauran kiya jane wala hai, toh woh aapko apne mind ke sath aishi cheezein karne kabil bana sakti hain jinhein aapne socha nahi hoga ki possible hain. Alternatively, unhein shuruati jankari haasil karne (information acquisition) ko smooth banane ke liye ek intermediate strategy ke roop mein use kiya ja sakta hai jab jankari kaafi dense ho. Maine unhein language learning aur terminology ke liye useful paaya hai, aur, SRS ke sath pair karne par, woh is ehsaas se ki koi rasta nahi hai jisse aap possibly har cheez ko yaad rakh sakein, ise itna gehrai se yaad rakhne ke beech ek effective bridge bana sakte hain ki aap possibly bhool na sakein. Indeed, paper, computers, aur doosre baari roop se tikne wali memories (externalized memories) se pehle ki duniya mein, mnemonics hi town mein mukhya game thin. Halanki, modern duniya mein, jisne is fact ke liye excellent coping mechanisms develop kiye hain ki zyaada tar log cheezon ko computer ki tarah yaad nahi rakh sakte, main feel karta hoon ki mnemonics seekhne ke aapke prayason ke aadhar ke roop mein kaam karne ke bajaye mazeed cool tricks ke roop mein serve karti hain. Phir bhi, ultralearners ka ek samarpit subset hai jo in techniques ko apply karne ke liye fiercely committed hai, isliye mere lafz final verdict nahi hone chahiye.

## Winning the War Against Forgetting

_(Bhoolne Ke Khilaf Jung Jeetna)_

Jankari ko retain karna ultimately bhoolne ki apariharya insani tendency (inevitable human tendency to forget) se ladna hai. Yeh process hum sab mein hoti hai, aur isse poori tarah se bachne ka koi tarika nahi hai. Halanki, khhas strategies—**spacing, proceduralization, overlearning, aur mnemonics**—bhoolne ki aapki short- aur long-term rates ka muqabla kar sakti hain aur aakhirkar aapki memorization mein ek vishal farq la sakti hain.

Maine is chapter ko Nigel Richards ki mysterious Scrabble mastery par discuss karke khola tha. Woh itne saare words ko itni jaldi recall karne aur unhein letters ke ek jumbled tiles ke set mein dekhne kabil kaise hain, yeh nishchit roop se ek enigma (paheli) bana rahega. Unke baare mein hum jo kuch bhi jaante hain woh doosre ultralearners ki picture mein fit baithta hai jinhone memory-intensive subjects par dominate kiya hai: **active recall, spaced rehearsal, aur intense practice ke prati ek dhun-bhara samarpan (obsessive commitment).** Chahe aapke ya mere paas Richards jitna door jaane ka will ho, yeh ek open question hai, lekin hard work aur ek achhi strategy ke sath, mujhe yeh likely lagta hai ki bhoolne ke khilaf jung ek haarne wali jung nahi honi chahiye.

Bhale hi Richards ki Scrabble practice unhein un words ko memorize karne ka benefit deti ho jinka matlab woh nahi jaante, real life ek different tarah ki memory ko reward karti hai: ek aishi memory jo knowledge ko cheezon ke ek gehre samajh (deep understanding) mein integrate karti hai. Agle niyan mein, hum memory se antardrishti (intuition) ki taraf badhne par dekhenge.

---

# Chapter 11 — Principle 8: Intuition

### _(Niyam 8 — Intuition: Upar Build Karne Se Pehle Gehra Khodein)_

---

> _"Do not ask whether a statement is true until you know what it means."_
> _(Jab tak aapko yeh na pata ho ki kisi kathan [statement] ka matlab kya hai, tab tak yeh mat poochiye ki kya woh sach hai.)_
> — Errett Bishop, mathematician

---

Duniya ke liye, woh ek ajeeb (eccentric) professor aur Nobel Prize–winning physicist the; unke biographer ke liye, woh ek genius the; lekin jo unhein jaante the, unke liye Richard Feynman ek jaadugar (magician) the. Unke saathi mathematician Mark Kac ne ek baar prastavit (posited) kiya tha ki duniya mein do tarah ke geniuses hote hain. Pehle ordinary geniuses hote hain: “Ek baar jab hum samajh jaate hain ki unhone kya kiya hai, toh hamein yakeen ho jata hai ki hum bhi aisa kar sakte the.” Doosri tarah ke magicians hote hain, jinka mind itne rahasyamai tareeqon (inscrutable ways) se kaam karta hai ki “Unke kaam ko samajhne ke baad bhi, jis process se unhone ise kiya hai woh poori tarah andhera (dark) rehti hai.” Kac ke hisab se, Feynman “sabse oonche darje ke jaadugar (a magician of the highest caliber)” the.

Feynman un problems ko le sakte the jinpar doosron ne mahino kaam kiya ho aur immediately unka solution dekh sakte the. High school mein, woh mathematics tournaments mein compete karte the, jahan woh aksar tabhi sahi answer de dete the jab problem abhi bataya hi ja raha hota tha. Jab unke competitors ne abhi calculate (compute) karna shuru hi kiya hota, Feynman ka answer pehle se hi page par circled hota tha. College ke dino mein, unhone _Putnam Mathematics Competition_ mein compete kiya, jisme winner ke liye Harvard ki paid scholarship milti thi. Yeh competition badnam roop se difficult (notoriously difficult) hai, jisme seedhe-saaf tareeqon ke bajaye chalaak rannitiyon (clever tricks) ki zarurat hoti hai. Samay bhi ek factor hota hai, aur kuch exam sessions ka madhyika score (median score) zero hota hai, jiska matlab hai ki typical pratiyogi ek bhi sahi answer nahi de pata. Feynman exam se jaldi baahar chale gaye. Unhone first place haasil kiya, aur unke fraternity brothers baad mein Feynman ke score aur list mein agle char logon ke score ke beech ke vishal farq (drastic gap) ko dekhkar hairan reh gaye. Manhattan Project par unke kaam ke dauran, Niels Bohr ne, jo us samay ke sabse famous aur important physicists mein se ek the, doosre physicists se baat karne se pehle is young grad student ke samne apne ideas ko rakhne (run his ideas by) ke liye Feynman se directly baat karne ko kaha. “Wahi ek akela banda hai jo mujhse nahi darrta,” Bohr ka explanation tha. “Jab mere paas koi crazy idea hota hai toh [woh] keh deta hai.”

Na hi Feynman ka yeh jaadu sirf physics tak seemit tha. Bachpan mein woh logon ke radios theek karne jaate the, aashik roop se isliye kyunki Depression ke dauran repairs ke liye kisi adult ko pay karna bahut costly tha, lekin isliye bhi kyunki radio ke owners unki process par hairan (marveled) hote the. Ek baar, jab woh gehre vicharon mein doobe (lost in thought) yeh figure out karne ki koshish kar rahe the ki ek radio start hote waqt ek kharab noise kyun produce kar raha tha, toh radio ka owner be-sabr (impatient) ho gaya. “Aap kya kar rahe hain? Aap radio fix karne aaye hain, lekin aap sirf aage-peeche chal rahe hain!” “Main soch raha hoon!” javab aaya, jispar owner Feynman ki us nidarrta (boldness) par hairan hote hue hans pada jiske liye woh baad mein famous hue. “Yeh soch kar radios fix karta hai!”

Manhattan Project mein atomic bomb ke nirman (construction) ke dauran ek young man ke roop mein, woh apne free time mein apne supervisors ke desks aur cabinets ke locks pick karne mein bitaate the. Unhone ek baar ek practical joke ke roop mein apne ek senior colleague ke filing cabinet ko break into (toda) kiya, jahan nuclear bomb banane ke secrets rakkhe gaye the. Ek aur baar, unhone ek military official ko apni technique demonstrate ki, jisne security flaw ko theek karne ke bajaye, sabko warn karna sahi samjha ki Feynman ko unke safes se door rakkha jaye! Baad mein, ek locksmith se milne par, unhone paaya ki unki reputation is had tak badh gayi thi ki us professional ne kaha, “God! Aap Feynman hain—bade safecracker (tijori todne wale)!”

Unhone ek human calculator hone ka impression bhi create kiya. Brazil ke ek trip par, woh ek abacus (ginatara) salesman ke samne aamne-saamne (toe to toe) gaye, 1,729.03 ke cube root jaise difficult figures ko calculate (computing) karte hue. Na keval Feynman ko sahi answer mila, 12.002, balki unhein abacus salesman ke mukable mazeed decimal places tak mila, jo abhi bhi tezi se calculate kar raha tha jab Feynman ne apna paanch-digit ka result display kar diya. Is ability ne doosre professional mathematicians ko bhi impress kiya, jinse unhone tark diya ki woh, ek minute ke andar, kisi bhi aise problem ka answer de sakte hain jise das seconds mein bataya ja sake, sahi number ke 10 percent ke andar. Mathematicians ne unpar sawaal phenke jaise “e to the power of 3.3” ya “e to the power of 1.4,” aur Feynman sahi answer lagbhag immediately wapas ugalne (spit back) mein kabil rahe.

## Demystifying Feynman’s Magic

_(Feynman Ke Jaadu Se Parda Hatana)_

Feynman nishchit roop se ek genius the. Kai log, unke biographer James Gleick ko shamil karte hue, ise yahin chhodne par santusht hain. Ek jaadu ka trick, akhirkar, sabse zyaada dazzling (chamkila/hairan karne wala) tabhi hota hai jab aap nahi jaante ki ise kaise kiya gya hai. Shayad yahi wajah hai ki is mard ke kai accounts ne unke method ke bajaye unke jaadu par focus kiya hai.

Bhale hi Feynman kaafi smart the, unke jaadu mein kuch gaps the. Woh math aur physics mein toh behtar the lekin humanities (manaviki) mein behad kharab (abysmal) the. History mein unke college ke grades unki class ke bottom ke panchve hisse (bottom fifth) mein the, literature mein bottom ke chhathe hisse (bottom sixth) mein the, aur unke fine arts ke grades unke saathi students ke 93 percent logon se badtar the. Ek point par, unhone pass hone ke liye ek test par cheating ka sahara (resorted to cheating) bhi liya. School mein unke adhyayan ke dauran maapi gayi unki intelligence ka score 125 tha. Ek average college graduate ka score 115 hota hai, jo Feynman ko unse sirf thoda sa hi upar (modestly higher) rakhta hai. Shayad, jaisa ki baad mein tark diya gaya hai, Feynman ka genius unke IQ score mein capture hone mein fail raha, ya yeh simply ek kharab tareeqe se liya gaya test tha. Halanki, ek aise insaan ke liye jise samajh se pare (beyond comprehension) mind ke liye itna celebrates kiya jata hai, yeh facts hamein yaad dilate hain ki Feynman ek sadharan insaan (mortal) the.

Feynman ke dimaagi hisab-kitab (mental calculus) ke baare mein kya? Is case mein, hamare paas Feynman ke khud ke lafz hain ki woh abacus salesman ya apne mathematician colleagues ke mukable itni tezi se kaise calculate kar sakte the. 1,729.03 ka cube root? Feynman ne explain kiya, “Mujhe sanyog se pata tha (I happened to know) ki ek cubic foot mein 1728 cubic inches hote hain, isliye answer 12 se thoda sa zyaada hai. Woh badhottari (excess), 1.03, lagbhag 2000 mein se sirf ek hissa hai, aur maine calculus mein seekha tha ki chote fractions ke liye, cube root ki excess number ki excess ka ek-tihaai (one-third) hoti hai. Toh mujhe bas fraction 1/1728 dhoondhna tha, aur 4 se multiply karna था.” Constant e to the power of 1.4? Feynman ne zahir kiya, “radioactivity ke kaaran, main base e par 2 ka log jaanta tha, jo .69315 hai (isliye main yeh bhi jaanta tha ki e to the power of .7 lagbhag 2 ke barabar hai).” 1.4 ki power par jaane ke liye, unhein bas us number ko apne aap se multiply karna tha. “Poori tarah kismat (sheer luck),” unhone explain kiya. Secret unki khhas arithmetic nateejon ke liye impressive memory aur numbers ke sath ek antardrishti (intuition) thi jisse woh interpolation (shabd-veshan) karne kabil the. Halanki, unke examiners ke lucky chunaav ne unhein calculate karne ki ek jaadui ability ka impression chhodne ki izazat di.
